Typically, this vector line element can be designated as etds, dr, or sometimes as tds, where et (or t) is a unit vector tangential to the curve, ds is the scalar line element, and dr is the differential of the position vector r describing the curve with respect to an origin point.Youline integral

		in a vector field, curve for which the tangent at each point carries the vector of the vector field quantity at that pointChatGPTChatGPTA field line, in the context of a vector field, is a curve or path within the field where the tangent vector at each point on the curve corresponds to the vector associated with the quantity of the vector field at that specific point. 		vector field characterized by a vector having zero rotation

Ostrogradsky theorem
		for a vector field U that is given at each point of a three-dimensional domain V limited by a closed surface S having an orientation towards exterior, theorem stating that the volume integral over V of the divergence of the field U is equal to the flux of this field through the surface S
â­VdivâUdV=â¯SUâendA

where dV is the volume element and endA is the vector surface element

Note 1 to entry: The divergence theorem can be generalized to the n-dimensional Euclidean space.

Note 2 to entry: In electrostatics, the divergence theorem is applied to express that the electric flux through a closed surface is equal to the total electric charge in the domain enclosed by the surface. It is then called "Gauss law".ChatGPTChatGPTThe divergence theorem, also known as Gauss's theorem or Ostrogradsky's theorem, is a fundamental theorem in vector calculus that applies to a vector field U defined at each point within a three-dimensional domain V, which is bounded by a closed surface S with an outward orientation. This theorem states that the volume integral over V of the divergence of the vector field U is equal to the flux of this field through the closed surface S. Note 1 to entry: It is equivalent to consider the n vectors associated with the columns.ChatGPTChatGPTA regular matrix, also known as a non-singular matrix or invertible matrix, is a square matrix of order "n" with elements Aij for which the n vectors Vi, formed by the rows or columns of the matrix, are linearly independent. In other words, the determinant of the matrix is nonzero.Here's what this definition means in more detail:"Square matrix of order n" refers to a matrix with the same number of rows and columns, and "n" represents the number of rows (which is also equal to the number of columns)."Linearly independent vectors" means that the vectors Vi formed by the rows or columns of the matrix cannot be expressed as linear combinations of each other. 		square matrix the elements of which have the property: Aij = Aji
Note 1 to entry: A symmetric matrix is equal to its transpose.

Note 2 to entry: All eigenvalues of a symmetric matrix with real elements are real.ChatGPTChatGPTA symmetric matrix is a square matrix where the elements are symmetric with respect to the main diagonal, meaning that Aij is equal to Aji for all elements of the matrix. In other words, if you were to reflect the matrix along its main diagonal, the elements on one side would match the corresponding elements on the other side.One notable property of symmetric matrices is that they are equal to their transpose. In mathematical notation, if A is a symmetric matrix, then A = A^T, where A^T represents the transpose of matrix A.Another important property is that all the eigenvalues of a symmetric matrix with real elements are real. This property has significant implications in various mathematical and scientific applications, including physics and engineering, where symmetric matrices often arise.Youorthogonal matrix
		square matrix A for which the inverse Aâ1 is equal to the transpose matrix AT
Note 1 to entry: For an orthogonal matrix with elements Aij:

âiAijAik=Î´jk
 and âkAikAjk=Î´ij

where Î´jk and Î´ij are Kronecker deltas.ChatGPTChatGPTAn orthogonal matrix is a square matrix A for which its inverse, denoted as A^(-1), is equal to its transpose, denoted as A^T. In other words, if A is an orthogonal matrix, then A^(-1) = A^T.Orthogonal matrices have a special property: when you multiply an orthogonal matrix by its transpose, the result is the identity matrix. This property can be expressed mathematically as follows:A^T * A = Iwhere A^T is the transpose of matrix A, A is the orthogonal matrix itself, and I is the identity matrix.Orthogonal matrices play a fundamental role in linear algebra and have applications in various fields, including computer graphics, signal processing, and robotics. They are commonly used for transformations that preserve lengths and angles, making them useful for tasks like rotations and reflections.YouHermitian matrix
		complex square matrix the elements of which have the property: Aij=Aâji
Note 1 to entry: A Hermitian matrix A is equal to its Hermitian conjugate matrix AH.

Note 2 to entry: All eigenvalues of a Hermitian matrix are real.

Note 3 to entry: Any symmetric matrix with real elements is a Hermitian matrix.

ChatGPTChatGPTA Hermitian matrix is a complex square matrix where the elements satisfy the property Aij = Aâji, which means that the elements are equal to the complex conjugates of each other when reflected across the main diagonal. In mathematical terms, if A is a Hermitian matrix, then Aij = Aâji for all elements i and j.Hermitian matrices are also referred to as self-adjoint matrices. They have several important properties:Hermitian matrices are equal to their Hermitian conjugate (adjoint) matrices: A = AH, where AH represents the Hermitian conjugate (transpose with complex conjugate) of matrix A.All eigenvalues of a Hermitian matrix are real numbers. This property makes Hermitian matrices particularly important in quantum mechanics and other areas of physics.Hermitian matrices are a generalization of symmetric matrices. If all elements of a Hermitian matrix are real, it becomes a symmetric matrix.Hermitian matrices have applications in various fields, including quantum mechanics, signal processing, and linear algebra. They play a crucial role in representing observables and operators in quantum mechanics due to their real eigenvalues, which correspond to measurable quantities in physical systems.Youunitary matrix
		regular square matrix A with complex elements for which the inverse Aâ1 is equal to the Hermitian conjugate matrix AH

âiAijAâik=Î´jk
 and âkAikAâjk=Î´ij

where Î´jk
 and Î´ij
 are Kronecker deltas.

Note 2 to entry: Any orthogonal matrix with real elements is a unitary matrix.ChatGPTChatGPTA unitary matrix is a square matrix with complex elements that has the property where its inverse is equal to the Hermitian conjugate (adjoint) of the matrix. In mathematical terms, if A is a unitary matrix, then A^(-1) = A^H, where A^H represents the Hermitian conjugate (transpose with complex conjugate) of matrix A.Unitary matrices have several important properties:Unitary matrices preserve the inner product of vectors. If you apply a unitary matrix to a vector, it will not change the length (norm) of the vector or the angles between vectors. This property is crucial in quantum mechanics and signal processing.All eigenvalues of a unitary matrix have absolute values equal to 1. In other words, unitary matrices represent transformations that preserve the lengths of vectors.Unitary matrices play a fundamental role in quantum mechanics, where they represent transformations of quantum states that conserve the probabilities of measurement outcomes.Any orthogonal matrix with real elements is a special case of a unitary matrix when dealing with real numbers.Unitary matrices are widely used in various areas of mathematics, physics, and engineering, particularly in the context of linear transformations that preserve the structure of vectors and complex numbers.Youpositive definite matrix
		Hermitian matrix A such that, for any non-zero column matrix U with complex elements, the 1 Ã 1 matrix UHAU has a unique element which is real and positive: (UHAU)11 > 0
Note 1 to entry: A symmetric matrix A with real elements is a positive definite matrix if UTAU > 0 for any non-zero column matrix U with real elements.

Note 2 to entry: All eigenvalues of a positive definite matrix are positive.

ChatGPTChatGPTA positive definite matrix is a special type of Hermitian matrix that has some important mathematical properties:For any non-zero column matrix U with complex elements, the quadratic form U^H A U results in a real and positive scalar, where U^H represents the Hermitian conjugate (adjoint) of U. In other words, the expression (U^H A U) is a real number greater than zero.In the case of a symmetric matrix A with real elements, it is considered positive definite if the quadratic form U^T A U is positive for any non-zero column matrix U with real elements.All eigenvalues of a positive definite matrix are real and positive. This property is essential in applications involving optimization, such as in the context of convex functions and the positive definiteness of Hessian matrices.Positive definite matrices are used in various mathematical and computational fields, including linear algebra, numerical analysis, optimization, and statistics. They play a fundamental role in defining inner products, inducing norms, and ensuring the convergence and stability of numerical algorithms.In machine learning and statistics, positive definite matrices are commonly encountered in the context of covariance matrices and kernel matrices, where they represent valid measures of similarity or distance.In summary, positive definite matrices are a specific class of Hermitian matrices with crucial properties related to real and positive eigenvalues, making them valuable in various mathematical and computational applications.YouThese terms are were from IEC electropedia:
